Task instruction sent to agent 
# Migration Guide: Envoy External Processing Filter (v1.30 → v1.31)

## Task

Generate a comprehensive migration guide for upgrading the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from **version 1.30.0 to version 1.31.0**.

## Context

The workspace contains two versions of the Envoy codebase:
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.30/` - Envoy v1.30.0 (April 2024)
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.31/` - Envoy v1.31.0 (July 2024)

## Scope

Focus specifically on the **External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter** configuration and implementation changes. This filter allows external services to process HTTP requests and responses.

Your migration guide should identify and document:

1. **Breaking Changes** - Incompatible configuration or behavioral changes
2. **Deprecated Features** - Fields or modes marked for future removal
3. **New Features** - Added capabilities and configuration options
4. **Configuration Updates** - Required or recommended changes to ext_proc filter configuration
5. **Behavioral Changes** - Modifications to filter behavior or runtime semantics

## Relevant Components

The ext_proc filter is primarily located in:
- Proto definitions: `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/`
- Implementation: `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/`
- Documentation: `docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst`

## Deliverable

Write your migration guide to `/workspace/documentation.md` in Markdown format with the following sections:

1. **Overview** - Summary of the migration and major changes
2. **Breaking Changes** - Critical incompatible changes requiring action
3. **Deprecated Features** - Features marked for deprecation with migration advice
4. **New Features** - New capabilities and how to use them
5. **Migration Steps** - Step-by-step instructions for upgrading configurations
6. **Testing Recommendations** - How to validate the migration
7. **Rollback Guidance** - How to revert if issues occur

## Requirements

- Provide specific proto field names and types
- Include before/after configuration examples for each breaking change
- Explain the motivation or benefit behind major changes
- Cite specific source files where implementations changed
- Recommend best practices for adopting new features
- Identify common migration pitfalls or edge cases

## Tips

- Compare the two version directories to identify changed proto fields and implementation files
- Search for all API modifications in the ext_proc filter
- Trace configuration usage patterns across both versions
- Look for related documentation updates

   105→
   106→// Replaces all entries with the same name or append one.
   107→void mergeHeaderValues(std::vector<envoy::config::core::v3::HeaderValue>& metadata,
   108→                       const envoy::config::core::v3::HeaderValue& header) {
   109→  bool has_key = false;
   110→  for (auto& dest : metadata) {
   111→    if (dest.key() == header.key()) {
   112→      dest.CopyFrom(header);
   113→      has_key = true;
   114→    }
   115→  }
   116→  if (!has_key) {
   117→    metadata.emplace_back(header);
   118→  }
   119→}
   120→
   121→std::vector<envoy::config::core::v3::HeaderValue>
   122→mergeGrpcInitialMetadata(const FilterConfigPerRoute& less_specific,
   123→                         const FilterConfigPerRoute& more_specific) {
   124→  std::vector<envoy::config::core::v3::HeaderValue> metadata(less_specific.grpcInitialMetadata());
   125→
   126→  for (const auto& header : more_specific.grpcInitialMetadata()) {
   127→    mergeHeaderValues(metadata, header);

     1→.. _config_http_filters_ext_proc:
     2→
     3→External Processing
     4→===================
     5→* This filter should be configured with the type URL ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor``.
     6→* :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`
     7→
     8→The external processing filter connects an external service, called an "external processor,"
     9→to the filter chain. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows
    10→it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining
    11→and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.
    12→
    13→The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the
    14→external processor
    15→:ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`
    16→messages, and the processor must reply with
    17→:ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`
    18→messages.
    19→
    20→Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.
    21→This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both
    22→request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration
    23→on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors
    24→that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary
    25→stream requests from the proxy.
    26→
    27→This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality
    28→are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementatio
... (truncated)

    22→// [#protodoc-title: External processing service]
    23→
    24→// A service that can access and modify HTTP requests and responses
    25→// as part of a filter chain.
    26→// The overall external processing protocol works like this:
    27→//
    28→// 1. Envoy sends to the service information about the HTTP request.
    29→// 2. The service sends back a ProcessingResponse message that directs Envoy
    30→//    to either stop processing, continue without it, or send it the
    31→//    next chunk of the message body.
    32→// 3. If so requested, Envoy sends the server chunks of the message body,
    33→//    or the entire body at once. In either case, the server sends back
    34→//    a ProcessingResponse after each message it receives.
    35→// 4. If so requested, Envoy sends the server the HTTP trailers,
    36→//    and the server sends back a ProcessingResponse.
    37→// 5. A
... (truncated)

  1195→  logGrpcStreamInfo();

  1198→    // The user would like a timeout to not cause message processing to fail.
  1199→    // However, we don't know if the external processor will send a response later,
  1200→    // and we can't wait any more. So, as we do for a spurious message, ignore

  1008→void Filter::onMessageTimeout() {
  1009→  ENVOY_LOG(debug, "message timeout reached");
  1010→  logGrpcStreamInfo();
  1011→  stats_.message_timeouts_.inc();
  1012→  if (config_->failureModeAllow()) {
  1013→    // The user would like a timeout to not cause message processing to fail.
  1014→    // However, we don't know if the external processor will send a response later,
  1015→    // and we can't wait any more. So, as we do for a spurious message, ignore
  1016→    // the external processor for the rest of the request.
  1017→    processing_complete_ = true;
  1018→    closeStream();
  1019→    stats_.failure_mode_allowed_.inc();
  1020→    clearAsyncState();
  1021→
  1022→  } else {
  1023→    // Return an error and stop processing the current stream.
  1024→    processing_complete_ = true;
  1025→    closeStream();
  1026→    decoding_state_.onFinishProcessorCall(Grpc::Status::DeadlineExceeded);
  1027→    encoding_state_.onFinishProcessorCall(Grpc::Status::DeadlineExceeded);
  1028→    ImmediateResponse errorResponse;
  1029→    errorResponse.mutable_status()->set_code(StatusCode::InternalServerError);
  1030→    errorResponse.set_details(absl::StrFormat("%s_per-message_timeout_exceeded", ErrorPrefix));
  1031→    sendImmediateResponse(errorResponse);
  1032→  }
  1033→}
  1034→
  1035→// Regardless of the current filter state, reset it to "IDLE", continue
  1036→// the current callback, and reset timers. This is used in a few error-handling situations.
  1037→void Filter::clearAsyncState() {

86-assistanttext-
The migration guide has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here is a summary of everything covered:

---

## Key Findings

### Breaking Changes

1. **Message timeout HTTP status code: 500 → 504**
   - `Filter::onMessageTimeout()` in `ext_proc.cc` now returns `GatewayTimeout` (504) instead of `InternalServerError` (500) when a per-message timeout expires. This is a behavioral fix — 504 is semantically correct for a timeout waiting on an upstream gRPC service.

2. **`ImmediateResponse.body` type: `string` → `bytes`**
   - In `api/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto`, field 3 of `ImmediateResponse` changed from `string` to `bytes`. Wire-compatible but requires updating generated language bindings and code that populates this field.

### Deprecated Features

3. **`disable_clear_route_cache` (field 11) is superseded by `route_cache_action` (field 18)**
   - Marked with `udpa.annotations.field_migrate` annotation. Setting both simultaneously throws a configuration error at startup.

### New Features

4. **`route_cache_action` enum** (field 18): `DEFAULT` / `CLEAR` / `RETAIN` — explicit, three-valued control over route cache behavior.

5. **`deferred_close_timeout`** (field 19): Controls how long observability-mode gRPC streams are held open after the HTTP stream ends. Default: 5 seconds.

6. **Observability mode fully implemented**: Deferred stream closure via `ThreadLocalStreamManager` and `DeferredDeletableStream`, safe callback invalidation via `OptRef`, `observability_mode = true` flag set in `ProcessingRequest`, and proper handling in body/header/trailer paths.

7. **`grpc_side_stream_flow_control` runtime flag**: New reloadable feature enabling watermark-based flow control on ext_proc gRPC side streams.

After the initial\n// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n// and how it should be processed.\n//\n// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n//\n// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n//   sent asynchronously.\n// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n//\n// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n// processor must send a matching response.\n//\n// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n//   to SEND.\n// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n//   request trailers.\n//\n// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n//\n// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n// sophisticated ways. For example:\n//\n// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n//   on the content of the headers.\n// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n//\n// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. The metadata\n  // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\n  // ext_proc filter name.\n  google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n\n  // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\n  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n  // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\n  // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\n  // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\n  bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n\n  // If set to true, ignore the\n  // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\n  // message in an external processor response. It is \"Send and Go\" mode that can be used\n  // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\n  //\n  // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\n  // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n  //\n  // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\n  // This also means that\n  // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n  // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\n  //\n  // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\n  //\n  // .. warning::\n  //\n  //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\n  //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\n  //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\n  //    discretion when enabling this feature.\n  //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\n  //\n  bool observability_mode = 17;\n}\n\n// The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\n// dynamic metadata. Specifically, which namespaces to send to the server, whether\n// metadata returned by the server may be written, and how that metadata may be written.\nmessage MetadataOptions {\n  message MetadataNamespaces {\n    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as an opaque *protobuf::Struct*.\n    repeated string untyped = 1;\n\n    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as a *protobuf::Any*. This allows\n    // envoy and the external processing server to share the protobuf message\n    // definition for safe parsing.\n    repeated string typed = 2;\n  }\n\n  // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to forward to\n  // the external processing server.\n  MetadataNamespaces forwarding_namespaces = 1;\n\n  // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to accept from\n  // the external processing server. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\n  // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\n  MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\n}\n\n// The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\n// allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n//\n// This works as below:\n//\n//   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\n//   2. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\n//      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n//   4. If ``disallowed_headers`` is set, and ``allowed_headers`` is not set, all headers except\n//      headers in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\nmessage HeaderForwardingRules {\n  // If set, specifically allow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n  // processing server. For example:\n//\n// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n//   on the content of the headers.\n// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n//\n// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n    // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n    // to true.\n    RETAIN = 2;\n  }\n\n  reserved 4;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n\n  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n  // downstream client will be reset.\n  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n\n  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n\n  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n  // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n    lte {seconds: 3600}\n    gte {}\n  }];\n\n  // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n  // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n  string stat_prefix = 8;\n\n  // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n  // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n  // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n  // with the header prefix set via\n  // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n  // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n  // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n  // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\n  // route to be recomputed, set the\n  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n  // field to true in the same response.\n  config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\n\n  // Specify the upper bound of\n  // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\n  // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\n  google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n    lte {seconds: 3600}\n    gte {}\n  }];\n\n  // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n  // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\n  HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\n\n  // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. The metadata\n  // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\n  // ext_proc filter name.\n  google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n\n  // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\n  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n  // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\n  // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\n  // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\n  bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n\n  // If set to true, ignore the\n  // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\n  // message in an external processor response. In such case, no local reply will be sent.\n  // Instead, the stream to the external processor will be closed. There will be no\n  // more external processing for this stream from now on.\n  bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n\n  // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n  MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n\n  // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\n  // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \"Send and Go\" mode that can be used\n  // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\n  //\n  // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\n  // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n  //\n  // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\n  // This also means that\n  // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n  // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\n  //\n  // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\n  //\n  // .. warning::\n  //\n  //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\n  //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\n  //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\n  //    discretion when enabling this feature.\n  //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\n  //\n  bool observability_mode = 17;\n\n  // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\n  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n  // field is set in an external processor response.\n  // Only one of ``disable_clear_route_cache`` or ``route_cache_action`` can be set.\n  // It is recommended to set ``route_cache_action`` which supersedes ``disable_clear_route_cache``.\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\n  // Specifies the action to be taken when an external processor response is\n  // received in response to request headers. It is recommended to set this field than set\n  // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`.\n  // Only one of ``disable_clear_route_cache`` or ``route_cache_action`` can be set.\n  RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\n  // Specifies the deferred closure timeout for gRPC stream that connects to external processor. Currently, the deferred stream closure\n  // is only used in :ref:`observability_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.observability_mode>`.\n  // In observability mode, gRPC streams may be held open to the external processor longer than the lifetime of the regular client to\n  // backend stream lifetime. In this case, Envoy will eventually timeout the external processor stream according to this time limit.\n  // The default value is 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds) if not specified.\n  google.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\n}\n\n// The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\n// dynamic metadata. Specifically, which namespaces to send to the server, whether\n// metadata returned by the server may be written, and how that metadata may be written.\nmessage MetadataOptions {\n  message MetadataNamespaces {\n    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as an opaque *protobuf::Struct*.\n    repeated string untyped = 1;\n\n    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as a *protobuf::Any*. This allows\n    // envoy and the external processing server to share the protobuf message\n    // definition for safe parsing.\n    repeated string typed = 2;\n  }\n\n  // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to forward to\n  // the external processing server.\n  MetadataNamespaces forwarding_namespaces = 1;\n\n  // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to accept from\n  // the external processing server. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\n  // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\n  MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\n}\n\n// The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\n// allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n//\n// This works as below:\n//\n//   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\n//   2. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\n//      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n//   3. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\n//      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n//   4. If ``disallowed_headers`` is set, and ``allowed_headers`` is not set, all headers except\n//      headers in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\nmessage HeaderForwardingRules {\n  // If set, specifically allow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n  // processing server. This can be overridden by the below ``disallowed_headers``.\n  type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher allowed_headers = 1;\n\n  // If set, specifically disallow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n  // processing server. This overrides the above ``allowed_headers`` if a header matches both.\n  type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher disallowed_headers = 2;\n}\n\n// Extra settings that may be added to per-route configuration for a\n// virtual host or cluster.\nmessage ExtProcPerRoute {\n  oneof override {\n    option (validate.required) = true;\n\n    // Disable the filter for this particular vhost or route.\n    // If disabled is specified in multiple per-filter-configs, the most specific one will be used.\n    bool disabled = 1 [(validate.rules).bool = {const: true}];\n\n    // Override aspects of the configuration for this route. A set of\n    // overrides in a more specific configuration will override a \"disabled\"\n    // flag set in a less-specific one.\n    ExtProcOverrides overrides = 2;\n  }\n}\n\n// Overrides that may be set on a per-route basis\n// [#next-free-field: 8]\nmessage ExtProcOverrides {\n  // Set a different processing mode for this route than the default.\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 1;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Set a different asynchronous processing option than the default.\n  bool async_mode = 2;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Set different optional attributes than the default setting of the\n  // ``request_attributes`` field.\n  repeated string request_attributes = 3;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Set different optional properties than the default setting of the\n  // ``response_attributes`` field.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 4;\n\n  // Set a different gRPC service for this route than the default.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 5;\n\n  // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n  // Lists of forwarding and receiving namespaces will be overridden in their entirety,\n  // meaning the most-specific config that specifies this override will be the final\n  // config used. It is the prerogative of the control plane to ensure this\n  // most-specific config contains the correct final overrides.\n  MetadataOptions metadata_options = 6;\n\n  // Additional metadata to include into streams initiated to the ext_proc gRPC\n  // service. By default, request and response headers are sent,\n    // while trailers are skipped.\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Send the header or trailer.\n    SEND = 1;\n\n    // Do not send the header or trailer.\n    SKIP = 2;\n  }\n\n  // Control how the request and response bodies are handled\n  // When body mutation by external processor is enabled, ext_proc filter will always remove\n  // the content length header in three cases below because content length can not be guaranteed\n  // to be set correctly:\n  // 1) STREAMED BodySendMode: header processing completes before body mutation comes back.\n  // 2) BUFFERED_PARTIAL BodySendMode: body is buffered and could be injected in different phases.\n  // 3) BUFFERED BodySendMode + SKIP HeaderSendMode: header processing (e.g., update content-length) is skipped.\n  //\n  // In Envoy's http1 codec implementation, removing content length will enable chunked transfer\n  // encoding whenever feasible. The recipient (either client or server) must be able\n  // to parse and decode the chunked transfer coding.\n  // (see `details in RFC9112 <https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc9112#section-7.1>`_).\n  //\n  // In BUFFERED BodySendMode + SEND HeaderSendMode, content length header is allowed but it is\n  // external processor's responsibility to set the content length correctly matched to the length\n  // of mutated body. If they don't match, the corresponding body mutation will be rejected and\n  // local reply will be sent with an error message.\n  enum BodySendMode {\n    // Do not send the body at all. This is the default.\n    NONE = 0;\n\n    // Stream the body to the server in pieces as they arrive at the\n    // proxy.\n    STREAMED = 1;\n\n    // Buffer the message body in memory and send the entire body at once.\n    // If the body exceeds the configured buffer limit, then the\n    // downstream system will receive an error.\n    BUFFERED = 2;\n\n    // Buffer the message body in memory and send the entire body in one\n    // chunk. If the body exceeds the configured buffer limit, then the body contents\n    // up to the buffer limit will be sent.\n    BUFFERED_PARTIAL = 3;\n  }\n\n  // How to handle the request header. Default is \"SEND\".\n  HeaderSendMode request_header_mode = 1 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n\n  // How to handle the response header. Default is \"SEND\".\n  HeaderSendMode response_header_mode = 2 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n\n  // How to handle the request body. Default is \"NONE\".\n  BodySendMode request_body_mode = 3 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n\n  // How do handle the response body. Default is \"NONE\".\n  BodySendMode response_body_mode = 4 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n\n  // How to handle the request trailers. Default is \"SKIP\".\n  HeaderSendMode request_trailer_mode = 5 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n\n  // How to handle the response trailers. Default is \"SKIP\".\n  HeaderSendMode response_trailer_mode = 6 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n}\n",

    config.overrides().grpc_initial_metadata().end()),\n      untyped_forwarding_namespaces_(initUntypedForwardingNamespaces(config)),\n      typed_forwarding_namespaces_(initTypedForwardingNamespaces(config)),\n      untyped_receiving_namespaces_(initUntypedReceivingNamespaces(config)) {}\n\nFilterConfigPerRoute::FilterConfigPerRoute(const FilterConfigPerRoute& less_specific,\n                                           const FilterConfigPerRoute& more_specific)\n    : disabled_(more_specific.disabled()),\n      processing_mode_(mergeProcessingMode(less_specific, more_specific)),\n      grpc_service_(more_specific.grpcService().has_value() ? more_specific.grpcService()\n                                                            : less_specific.grpcService()),\n      grpc_initial_metadata_(mergeGrpcInitialMetadata(less_specific, more_specific)),\n      untyped_forwarding_namespaces_(more_specific.untypedForwardingMetadataNamespaces().has_value()\n                                         ? more_specific.untypedForwardingMetadataNamespaces()\n                                         : less_specific.untypedForwardingMetadataNamespaces()),\n      typed_forwarding_namespaces_(more_specific.typedForwardingMetadataNamespaces().has_value()\n                                       ? more_specific.typedForwardingMetadataNamespaces()\n                                       : less_specific.typedForwardingMetadataNamespaces()),\n      untyped_receiving_namespaces_(more_specific.untypedReceivingMetadataNamespaces().has_value()\n                                        ? more_specific.untypedReceivingMetadataNamespaces()\n                                        : less_specific.untypedReceivingMetadataNamespaces()) {}\n\nvoid Filter::setDecoderFilterCallbacks(Http::StreamDecoderFilterCallbacks& callbacks) {\n  Http::PassThroughFilter::setDecoderFilterCallbacks(callbacks);\n  decoding_state_.setDecoderFilterCallbacks(callbacks);\n  const Envoy::StreamInfo::FilterStateSharedPtr& filter_state =\n      callbacks.streamInfo().filterState();\n  if (!filter_state->hasData<ExtProcLoggingInfo>(callbacks.filterConfigName())) {\n    filter_state->setData(callbacks.filterConfigName(),\n                          std::make_shared<ExtProcLoggingInfo>(config_->filterMetadata()),\n                          Envoy::StreamInfo::FilterState::StateType::Mutable,\n                          Envoy::StreamInfo::FilterState::LifeSpan::Request);\n  }\n  logging_info_ = filter_state->getDataMutable<ExtProcLoggingInfo>(callbacks.filterConfigName());\n}\n\nvoid Filter::setEncoderFilterCallbacks(Http::StreamEncoderFilterCallbacks& callbacks) {\n  Http::PassThroughFilter::setEncoderFilterCallbacks(callbacks);\n  encoding_state_.setEncoderFilterCallbacks(callbacks);\n}\n\nFilter::StreamOpenState Filter::openStream() {\n  // External processing is completed. This means there is no need to send any further\n  // message to the server for processing. Just return IgnoreError so the filter\n  // will return FilterHeadersStatus::Continue.\n  if (processing_complete_) {\n    ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"External processing is completed when trying to open the gRPC stream\");\n    return StreamOpenState::IgnoreError;\n  }\n  if (!stream_) {\n    ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Opening gRPC stream to external processor\");\n    stream_ = client_->start(*this, config_with_hash_key_, decoder_callbacks_->streamInfo());\n    if (processing_complete_) {\n      // Stream failed while starting and either onGrpcError or onGrpcClose was already called\n      // Asserts that `stream_` is nullptr since it is not valid to be used any further\n      // beyond this point.\n      ASSERT(stream_ == nullptr);\n      return sent_immediate_response_ ? StreamOpenState::Error : StreamOpenState::IgnoreError;\n    }\n    stats_.streams_started_.inc();\n    // For custom access logging purposes. Applicable only for Envoy gRPC as Google gRPC does not\n    // have a proper implementation of streamInfo.\n    if (grpc_service_.has_envoy_grpc() && logging_info_ != nullptr) {\n      logging_info_->setClusterInfo(stream_->streamInfo().upstreamClusterInfo());\n    }\n  }\n  return StreamOpenState::Ok;\n}\n\nvoid Filter::closeStream() {\n  if (stream_) {\n    ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Calling close on stream\");\n    if (stream_->close()) {\n      stats_.streams_closed_.inc();\n    }\n    stream_.reset();\n  } else {\n    ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Stream already closed\");\n  }\n}\n\nvoid Filter::onDestroy() {\n  ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"onDestroy\");\n  // Make doubly-sure we no longer use the stream, as\n  // per the filter contract.\n  processing_complete_ = true;\n  closeStream();\n  decoding_state_.stopMessageTimer();\n  encoding_state_.stopMessageTimer();\n}\n\nFilterHeadersStatus Filter::onHeaders(ProcessorState& state,\n                                      Http::RequestOrResponseHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream) {\n  switch (openStream()) {\n  case StreamOpenState::Error:\n    return FilterHeadersStatus::StopIteration;\n  case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\n    return FilterHeadersStatus::Continue;\n  case StreamOpenState::Ok:\n    // Fall through\n    break;\n  }\n\n  state.setHeaders(&headers);\n  state.setHasNoBody(end_stream);\n  ProcessingRequest req;\n  addAttributes(state, req);\n  addDynamicMetadata(state, req);\n  auto* headers_req = state.mutableHeaders(req);\n  MutationUtils::headersToProto(headers, config_->allowedHeaders(), config_->disallowedHeaders(),\n                                *headers_req->mutable_headers());\n  headers_req->set_end_of_stream(end_stream);\n  state.onStartProcessorCall(std::bind(&Filter::onMessageTimeout, this), config_->messageTimeout(),\n                             ProcessorState::CallbackState::HeadersCallback);\n  ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Sending headers message\");\n  stream_->send(std::move(req), false);\n  stats_.stream_msgs_sent_.inc();\n  state.setPaused(true);\n  return FilterHeadersStatus::StopIteration;\n}\n\nFilterHeadersStatus Filter::decodeHeaders(RequestHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream) {\n  ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"decodeHeaders: end_stream = {}\", end_stream);\n  mergePerRouteConfig();\n  if (end_stream) {\n    decoding_state_.setCompleteBodyAvailable(true);\n  }\n\n  // Set the request headers on decoding and encoding state in case they are\n  // needed later.\n  decoding_state_.setRequestHeaders(&headers);\n  encoding_state_.setRequestHeaders(&headers);\n\n  FilterHeadersStatus status = FilterHeadersStatus::Continue;\n  if (decoding_state_.sendHeaders()) {\n    status = onHeaders(decoding_state_, headers, end_stream);\n    ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"onHeaders returning {}\", static_cast<int>(status));\n  } else {\n    ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"decodeHeaders: Skipped header processing\");\n  }\n\n  if (!processing_complete_ && decoding_state_.shouldRemoveContentLength()) {\n    headers.removeContentLength();\n  }\n  return status;\n}\n\nFilterDataStatus Filter::onData(ProcessorState& state, Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream) {\n  if (end_stream) {\n    state.setCompleteBodyAvailable(true);\n  }\n  if (state.bodyReplaced()) {\n    ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Clearing body chunk because CONTINUE_AND_REPLACE was returned\");\n    data.drain(data.length());\n    return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n  }\n  if (processing_complete_) {\n    ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Continuing (processing complete)\");\n    return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n  }\n\n  if (state.callbackState() == ProcessorState::CallbackState::HeadersCallback) {\n    ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Header processing still in progress -- holding body data\");\n    // We don't know what to do with the body until the response comes back.\n    // We must buffer it in case we need it when that happens.\n    // Raise a watermark to prevent a buffer overflow until the response comes back.\n    // When end_stream is true, we need to StopIterationAndWatermark as well to stop the\n    // ActiveStream from returning error when the last chunk added to stream buffer exceeds the\n    // buffer limit.\n    state.setPaused(true);\n    state.requestWatermark();\n    return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationAndWatermark;\n  }\n\n  FilterDataStatus result;\n  switch (state.bodyMode()) {\n  case ProcessingMode::BUFFERED:\n    if (end_stream) {\n      switch (openStream()) {\n      case StreamOpenState::Error:\n        return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n      case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\n        return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n      case StreamOpenState::Ok:\n        // Fall through\n        break;\n      }\n\n      // The body has been buffered and we need to send the buffer\n      ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Sending request body message\");\n      state.addBufferedData(data);\n      auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, *state.bufferedData(), end_stream);\n      sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::BufferedBodyCallback, req);\n      // Since we just just moved the data into the buffer, return NoBuffer\n      // so that we do not buffer this chunk twice.\n      state.setPaused(true);\n      result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n      break;\n    }\n    ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"onData: Buffering\");\n    state.setPaused(true);\n    result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationAndBuffer;\n    break;\n  case ProcessingMode::STREAMED: {\n    // STREAMED body mode works as follows:\n    //\n    // 1) As data callbacks come in to the filter, it \"moves\" the data into a new buffer, which it\n    // dispatches via gRPC message to the external processor, and then keeps in a queue. It\n    // may request a watermark if the queue is higher than the buffer limit to prevent running\n    // out of memory.\n    // 2) As a result, filters farther down the chain see empty buffers in some data callbacks.\n    // 3) When a response comes back from the external processor, it injects the processor's result\n    // into the filter chain using \"inject**codedData\". (The processor may respond indicating that\n    // there is no change, which means that the original buffer stored in the queue is what gets\n    // injected.)\n    //\n    // This way, we pipeline data from the proxy to the external processor, and give the processor\n    // the ability to modify each chunk, in order. Doing this any other way would have required\n    // substantial changes to the filter manager. See\n    // https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/16760 for a discussion.\n    switch (openStream()) {\n    case StreamOpenState::Error:\n      return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n    case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\n      return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n    case StreamOpenState::Ok:\n      // Fall through\n      break;\n    }\n\n    // Need to first enqueue the data into the chunk queue before sending.\n    auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, data, end_stream);\n    state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\n    sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::StreamedBodyCallback, req);\n\n    // At this point we will continue, but with no data, because that will come later\n    if (end_stream) {\n      // But we need to stop iteration for the last chunk because it's our last chance to do stuff\n      state.setPaused(true);\n      result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n    } else {\n      result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n    }\n    break;\n  }\n  case ProcessingMode::BUFFERED_PARTIAL:\n    // BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode works as follows:\n    //\n    // 1) As data chunks arrive, we move the data into a new buffer, which we store\n    // in the buffer queue, and continue the filter stream with an empty buffer. This\n    // is the same thing that we do in STREAMING mode.\n    // 2) If end of stream is reached before the queue reaches the buffer limit, we\n    // send the buffered data to the server and essentially behave as if we are in\n    // buffered mode.\n    // 3) If instead the buffer limit is reached before end of stream, then we also\n    // send the buffered data to the server, and raise the watermark to prevent Envoy\n    // from running out of memory while we wait.\n    // 4) It is possible that Envoy will keep sending us data even in that case, so\n    // we must continue to queue data and prepare to re-inject it later.\n    if (state.partialBodyProcessed()) {\n      // We already sent and received the buffer, so everything else just falls through.\n      ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Partial buffer limit reached\");\n      // Make sure that we do not accidentally try to modify the headers before\n      // we continue, which will result in them possibly being sent.\n      state.setHeaders(nullptr);\n      result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n    } else if (state.callbackState() ==\n               ProcessorState::CallbackState::BufferedPartialBodyCallback) {\n      // More data came in while we were waiting for a callback result. We need\n      // to queue it and deliver it later in case the callback changes the data.\n      state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\n      ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Call in progress for partial mode\");\n      state.setPaused(true);\n      result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n    } else {\n      state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\n      if (end_stream || state.queueOverHighLimit()) {\n        // At either end of stream or when the buffer is full, it's time to send what we have\n        // to the processor.\n        bool terminate;\n        FilterDataStatus chunk_result;\n        std::tie(terminate, chunk_result) = sendStreamChunk(state);\n        if (terminate) {\n          return chunk_result;\n        }\n      }\n      result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n    }\n    break;\n  case ProcessingMode::NONE:\n  default:\n    result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n    break;\n  }\n\n  return result;\n}\n\nstd::pair<bool, Http::FilterDataStatus> Filter::sendStreamChunk(ProcessorState& state) {\n  switch (openStream()) {\n  case StreamOpenState::Error:\n    return {true, FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer};\n  case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\n    return {true, FilterDataStatus::Continue};\n  case StreamOpenState::Ok:\n    // Fall through\n    break;\n  }\n\n  const auto& all_data = state.consolidateStreamedChunks();\n  ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Sending {} bytes of data in buffered partial mode. end_stream = {}\",\n            state.chunkQueue().receivedData().length(), all_data.end_stream);\n  auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, state.chunkQueue().receivedData(), all_data.end_stream);\n  sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::BufferedPartialBodyCallback, req);\n  state.setPaused(true);\n  return {false, FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer};\n}\n\nFilterDataStatus Filter::decodeData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream) {\n  ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"decodeData({}): end_stream = {}\", data.length(), end_stream);\n  const auto status = onData(decoding_state_, data, end_stream);\n  ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"decodeData returning {}\", static_cast<int>(status));\n  return status;\n}\n\nFilterTrailersStatus Filter::onTrailers(ProcessorState& state, Http::HeaderMap& trailers) {\n  if (processing_complete_) {\n    ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"trailers: Continue\");\n    return FilterTrailersStatus::Continue;\n  }\n\n  bool body_delivered = state.completeBodyAvailable();\n  state.setCompleteBodyAvailable(true);\n  state.setTrailersAvailable(true);\n  state.setTrailers(&trailers);\n\n  if (state.callbackState() != ProcessorState::CallbackState::Idle) {\n    ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Previous callback still executing -- holding header iteration\");\n    state.setPaused(true);\n    return FilterTrailersStatus::StopIteration;\n  }\n\n  if (!body_delivered &&\n      ((state.bufferedData() && state.bodyMode() == ProcessingMode::BUFFERED) ||\n       (!state.chunkQueue().empty() && state.bodyMode() == ProcessingMode::BUFFERED_PARTIAL))) {\n    // If no gRPC stream yet, opens it before sending data.\n    switch (openStream()) {\n    case StreamOpenState::Error:\n      return FilterTrailersStatus::StopIteration;\n    case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\n      return FilterTrailersStatus::Continue;\n    case StreamOpenState::Ok:\n      // Fall through\n      break;\n    }\n\n    // We would like to process the body in a buffered way, but until now the complete\n    // body has not arrived. With the arrival of trailers, we now know that the body\n    // has arrived.\n    if (state.bodyMode() == ProcessingMode::BUFFERED) {\n      // Sending data left over in the buffer.\n      auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, *state.bufferedData(), false);\n      sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::BufferedBodyCallback, req);\n    } else {\n      // Sending data left over in the queue.\n      const auto& all_data = state.consolidateStreamedChunks();\n      auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, state.chunkQueue().receivedData(), false);\n      ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Sending {} bytes of data in buffered partial mode. end_stream = {}\",\n                state.chunkQueue().receivedData().length(), all_data.end_stream);\n      sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::BufferedPartialBodyCallback, req);\n    }\n    state.setPaused(true);\n    return FilterTrailersStatus::StopIteration;\n  }\n\n  if (!state.sendTrailers()) {\n    ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Skipped trailer processing\");\n    return FilterTrailersStatus::Continue;\n  }\n\n  switch (openStream()) {\n  case StreamOpenState::Error:\n    return FilterTrailersStatus::StopIteration;\n  case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\n    return FilterTrailersStatus::Continue;\n  case StreamOpenState::Ok:\n    // Fall through\n    break;\n  }\n\n  sendTrailers(state, trailers);\n  state.setPaused(true);\n  return FilterTrailersStatus::StopIteration;\n}\n\nFilterTrailersStatus Filter::decodeTrailers(RequestTrailerMap& trailers) {\n  ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"decodeTrailers\");\n  const auto status = onTrailers(decoding_state_, trailers);\n  ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"decodeTrailers returning {}\", static_cast<int>(status));\n  return status;\n}\n\nFilterHeadersStatus Filter::encodeHeaders(ResponseHeaderMap& headers, bool end_stream) {\n  ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"encodeHeaders end_stream = {}\", end_stream);\n  // Try to merge the route config again in case the decodeHeaders() is not called when processing\n  // local reply.\n  mergePerRouteConfig();\n  if (end_stream) {\n    encoding_state_.setCompleteBodyAvailable(true);\n  }\n\n  FilterHeadersStatus status = FilterHeadersStatus::Continue;\n  if (!processing_complete_ && encoding_state_.sendHeaders()) {\n    status = onHeaders(encoding_state_, headers, end_stream);\n    ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"onHeaders returns {}\", static_cast<int>(status));\n  } else {\n    ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"encodeHeaders: Skipped header processing\");\n  }\n\n  // The content-length header will be kept when either one of the following conditions is met:\n  // (1) `shouldRemoveContentLength` returns false.\n  // (2) side stream processing has been completed. For example, it could be caused by stream error\n  // that triggers the local reply or due to spurious message that skips the side stream\n  // mutation.\n  if (!processing_complete_ && encoding_state_.shouldRemoveContentLength()) {\n    headers.removeContentLength();\n  }\n  return status;\n}\n\nFilterDataStatus Filter::encodeData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream) {\n  ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"encodeData({}): end_stream = {}\", data.length(), end_stream);\n  const auto status = onData(encoding_state_, data, end_stream);\n  ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"encodeData returning {}\", static_cast<int>(status));\n  return status;\n}\n\nFilterTrailersStatus Filter::encodeTrailers(ResponseTrailerMap& trailers) {\n  ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"encodeTrailers\");\n  const auto status = onTrailers(encoding_state_, trailers);\n  ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"encodeTrailers returning {}\", static_cast<int>(status));\n  return status;\n}\n\nProcessingRequest Filter::setupBodyChunk(ProcessorState& state, const Buffer::Instance& data,\n                                         bool end_stream) {\n  ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Sending a body chunk of {} bytes, end_stream {}\", data.length(), end_stream);\n  ProcessingRequest req;\n  addAttributes(state, req);\n  addDynamicMetadata(state, req);\n  auto* body_req = state.mutableBody(req);\n  body_req->set_end_of_stream(end_stream);\n  body_req->set_body(data.toString());\n  return req;\n}\n\nvoid Filter::sendBodyChunk(ProcessorState& state, ProcessorState::CallbackState new_state,\n                           ProcessingRequest& req) {\n  state.onStartProcessorCall(std::bind(&Filter::onMessageTimeout, this), config_->messageTimeout(),\n                             new_state);\n  stream_->send(std::move(req), false);\n  stats_.stream_msgs_sent_.inc();\n}\n\nvoid Filter::sendTrailers(ProcessorState& state, const Http::HeaderMap& trailers) {\n  ProcessingRequest req;\n  addAttributes(state, req);\n  addDynamicMetadata(state, req);\n  auto* trailers_req = state.mutableTrailers(req);\n  MutationUtils::headersToProto(trailers, config_->allowedHeaders(), config_->disallowedHeaders(),\n                                *trailers_req->mutable_trailers());\n  state.onStartProcessorCall(std::bind(&Filter::onMessageTimeout, this), config_->messageTimeout(),\n                             ProcessorState::CallbackState::TrailersCallback);\n  ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Sending trailers message\");\n  stream_->send(std::move(req), false);\n  stats_.stream_msgs_sent_.inc();\n}\n\nvoid Filter::logGrpcStreamInfo() {\n  if (stream_ != nullptr && logging_info_ != nullptr && grpc_service_.has_envoy_grpc()) {\n    const auto& upstream_meter = stream_->streamInfo().getUpstreamBytesMeter();\n    if (upstream_meter != nullptr) {\n      logging_info_->setBytesSent(upstream_meter->wireBytesSent());\n      logging_info_->setBytesReceived(upstream_meter->wireBytesReceived());\n    }\n    // Only set upstream host in logging info once.\n    if (logging_info_->upstreamHost() == nullptr) {\n      logging_info_->setUpstreamHost(stream_->streamInfo().upstreamInfo()->upstreamHost());\n    }\n  }\n}\n\nvoid Filter::onNewTimeout(const ProtobufWkt::Duration& override_message_timeout) {\n  const auto result = DurationUtil::durationToMillisecondsNoThrow(override_message_timeout);\n  if (!result.ok()) {\n    ENVOY_LOG(warn, \"Ext_proc server new timeout setting is out of duration range. \"\n                    \"Ignoring the message.\");\n    stats_.override_message_timeout_ignored_.inc();\n    return;\n  }\n  const auto message_timeout_ms = result.value();\n  // The new timeout has to be >=1ms and <= max_message_timeout configured in filter.\n  const uint64_t min_timeout_ms = 1;\n  const uint64_t max_timeout_ms = config_->maxMessageTimeout();\n  if (message_timeout_ms < min_timeout_ms || message_timeout_ms > max_timeout_ms) {\n    ENVOY_LOG(warn, \"Ext_proc server new timeout setting is out of config range. \"\n                    \"Ignoring the message.\");\n    stats_.override_message_timeout_ignored_.inc();\n    return;\n  }\n  // One of the below function call is non-op since the ext_proc filter can\n  // only be in one of the below state, and just one timer is enabled.\n  auto decoder_timer_restarted = decoding_state_.restartMessageTimer(message_timeout_ms);\n  auto encoder_timer_restarted = encoding_state_.restartMessageTimer(message_timeout_ms);\n  if (!decoder_timer_restarted && !encoder_timer_restarted) {\n    stats_.override_message_timeout_ignored_.inc();\n    return;\n  }\n  stats_.override_message_timeout_received_.inc();\n}\n\nvoid Filter::addDynamicMetadata(const ProcessorState& state, ProcessingRequest& req) {\n  // get the callbacks from the ProcessorState. This will be the appropriate\n  // callbacks for the current state of the filter\n  auto* cb = state.callbacks();\n  envoy::config::core::v3::Metadata forwarding_metadata;\n\n  // If metadata_context_namespaces is specified, pass matching filter metadata to the ext_proc\n  // service. If metadata key is set in both the connection and request metadata then the value\n  // will be the request metadata value. The metadata will only be searched for the callbacks\n  // corresponding to the traffic direction at the time of the external processing request.\n  const auto& request_metadata = cb->streamInfo().dynamicMetadata().filter_metadata();\n  for (const auto& context_key : state.untypedForwardingMetadataNamespaces()) {\n    if (const auto metadata_it = request_metadata.find(context_key);\n        metadata_it != request_metadata.end()) {\n      (*forwarding_metadata.mutable_filter_metadata())[metadata_it->first] = metadata_it->second;\n    } else if (cb->connection().has_value()) {\n      const auto& connection_metadata =\n          cb->connection().value().get().streamInfo().dynamicMetadata().filter_metadata();\n      if (const auto metadata_it = connection_metadata.find(context_key);\n          metadata_it != connection_metadata.end()) {\n        (*forwarding_metadata.mutable_filter_metadata())[metadata_it->first] = metadata_it->second;\n      }\n    }\n  }\n\n  // If typed_metadata_context_namespaces is specified, pass matching typed filter metadata to the\n  // ext_proc service. If metadata key is set in both the connection and request metadata then\n  // the value will be the request metadata value. The metadata will only be searched for the\n  // callbacks corresponding to the traffic direction at the time of the external processing\n  // request.\n  const auto& request_typed_metadata = cb->streamInfo().dynamicMetadata().typed_filter_metadata();\n  for (const auto& context_key : state.typedForwardingMetadataNamespaces()) {\n    if (const auto metadata_it = request_typed_metadata.find(context_key);\n        metadata_it != request_typed_metadata.end()) {\n      (*forwarding_metadata.mutable_typed_filter_metadata())[metadata_it->first] =\n          metadata_it->second;\n    } else if (cb->connection().has_value()) {\n      const auto& connection_typed_metadata =\n          cb->connection().value().get().streamInfo().dynamicMetadata().typed_filter_metadata();\n      if (const auto metadata_it = connection_typed_metadata.find(context_key);\n          metadata_it != connection_typed_metadata.end()) {\n        (*forwarding_metadata.mutable_typed_filter_metadata())[metadata_it->first] =\n            metadata_it->second;\n      }\n    }\n  }\n\n  *req.mutable_metadata_context() = forwarding_metadata;\n}\n\nvoid Filter::addAttributes(ProcessorState& state, ProcessingRequest& req) {\n  if (!state.sendAttributes(config_->expressionManager())) {\n    return;\n  }\n\n  auto activation_ptr = Filters::Common::Expr::createActivation(\n      &config_->expressionManager().localInfo(), state.callbacks()->streamInfo(),\n      state.requestHeaders(), dynamic_cast<const Http::ResponseHeaderMap*>(state.responseHeaders()),\n      dynamic_cast<const Http::ResponseTrailerMap*>(state.responseTrailers()));\n  auto attributes = state.evaluateAttributes(config_->expressionManager(), *activation_ptr);\n\n  state.setSentAttributes(true);\n  (*req.mutable_attributes())[FilterName] = attributes;\n}\n\nvoid Filter::setDynamicMetadata(Http::StreamFilterCallbacks* cb, const ProcessorState& state,\n                                const ProcessingResponse& response) {\n  if (state.untypedReceivingMetadataNamespaces().empty() || !response.has_dynamic_metadata()) {\n    if (response.has_dynamic_metadata()) {\n      ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"processing response included dynamic metadata, but no receiving \"\n                       \"namespaces are configured.\");\n    }\n    return;\n  }\n\n  auto response_metadata = response.dynamic_metadata().fields();\n  auto receiving_namespaces = state.untypedReceivingMetadataNamespaces();\n  for (const auto& context_key : response_metadata) {\n    bool found_allowed_namespace = false;\n    if (auto metadata_it =\n            std::find(receiving_namespaces.begin(), receiving_namespaces.end(), context_key.first);\n        metadata_it != receiving_namespaces.end()) {\n      cb->streamInfo().setDynamicMetadata(context_key.first,\n                                          response_metadata.at(context_key.first).struct_value());\n      found_allowed_namespace = true;\n    }\n    if (!found_allowed_namespace) {\n      ENVOY_LOG(debug,\n                \"processing response included dynamic metadata for namespace not \"\n                \"configured for receiving: {}\",\n                context_key.first);\n    }\n  }\n}\n\nvoid Filter::setEncoderDynamicMetadata(const ProcessingResponse& response) {\n  setDynamicMetadata(encoder_callbacks_, encoding_state_, response);\n}\nvoid Filter::setDecoderDynamicMetadata(const ProcessingResponse& response) {\n  setDynamicMetadata(decoder_callbacks_, decoding_state_, response);\n}\n\nvoid Filter::onReceiveMessage(std::unique_ptr<ProcessingResponse>&& r) {\n  if (processing_complete_) {\n    ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Ignoring stream message received after processing complete\");\n    // Ignore additional messages after we decided we were done with the stream\n    return;\n  }\n\n  auto response = std::move(r);\n\n  // Check whether the server is asking to extend the timer.\n  if (response->has_override_message_timeout()) {\n    onNewTimeout(response->override_message_timeout());\n    return;\n  }\n\n  // Update processing mode now because filter callbacks check it\n  // and the various \"handle\" methods below may result in callbacks\n  // being invoked in line. This only happens when filter has allow_mode_override\n  // set to true and filter is waiting for header processing response.\n  // Otherwise, the response mode_override proto field is ignored.\n  if (config_->allowModeOverride() && inHeaderProcessState() && response->has_mode_override()) {\n    ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Processing mode overridden by server for this request\");\n    decoding_state_.setProcessingMode(response->mode_override());\n    encoding_state_.setProcessingMode(response->mode_override());\n  }\n\n  ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Received {} response\", responseCaseToString(response->response_case()));\n  absl::Status processing_status;\n  switch (response->response_case()) {\n  case ProcessingResponse::ResponseCase::kRequestHeaders:\n    setDecoderDynamicMetadata(*response);\n    processing_status = decoding_state_.handleHeadersResponse(response->request_headers());\n    break;\n  case ProcessingResponse::ResponseCase::kResponseHeaders:\n    setEncoderDynamicMetadata(*response);\n    processing_status = encoding_state_.handleHeadersResponse(response->response_headers());\n    break;\n  case ProcessingResponse::ResponseCase::kRequestBody:\n    setDecoderDynamicMetadata(*response);\n    processing_status = decoding_state_.handleBodyResponse(response->request_body());\n    break;\n  case ProcessingResponse::ResponseCase::kResponseBody:\n    setEncoderDynamicMetadata(*response);\n    processing_status = encoding_state_.handleBodyResponse(response->response_body());\n    break;\n  case ProcessingResponse::ResponseCase::kRequestTrailers:\n    setDecoderDynamicMetadata(*response);\n    processing_status = decoding_state_.handleTrailersResponse(response->request_trailers());\n    break;\n  case ProcessingResponse::ResponseCase::kResponseTrailers:\n    setEncoderDynamicMetadata(*response);\n    processing_status = encoding_state_.handleTrailersResponse(response->response_trailers());\n    break;\n  case ProcessingResponse::ResponseCase::kImmediateResponse:\n    if (config_->disableImmediateResponse()) {\n      ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Filter has disable_immediate_response configured. \"\n                       \"Treat the immediate response message as spurious response.\");\n      processing_status =\n          absl::FailedPreconditionError(\"unhandled immediate response due to config disabled it\");\n    } else {\n      setDecoderDynamicMetadata(*response);\n      // We won't be sending anything more to the stream after we\n      // receive this message.\n      ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Sending immediate response\");\n      processing_complete_ = true;\n      onFinishProcessorCalls(Grpc::Status::Ok);\n      closeStream();\n      sendImmediateResponse(response->immediate_response());\n      processing_status = absl::OkStatus();\n    }\n    break;\n  default:\n    // Any other message is considered spurious\n    ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Received unknown stream message {} -- ignoring and marking spurious\",\n              response->response_case());\n    processing_status = absl::FailedPreconditionError(\"unhandled message\");\n    break;\n  }\n\n  if (processing_status.ok()) {\n    stats_.stream_msgs_received_.inc();\n  } else if (absl::IsFailedPrecondition(processing_status)) {\n    // Processing code uses this specific error code in the case that a\n    // message was received out of order.\n    stats_.spurious_msgs_received_.inc();\n    // When a message is received out of order, ignore it and also\n    // ignore the stream for the rest of this filter instance's lifetime\n    // to protect us from a malformed server.\n    ENVOY_LOG(warn, \"Spurious response message {} received on gRPC stream\",\n              response->response_case());\n    closeStream();\n    clearAsyncState();\n    processing_complete_ = true;\n  } else {\n    // Any other error results in an immediate response with an error message.\n    // This could happen, for example, after a header mutation is rejected.\n    ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Sending immediate response: {}\", processing_status.message());\n    stats_.stream_msgs_received_.inc();\n    processing_complete_ = true;\n    onFinishProcessorCalls(processing_status.raw_code());\n    closeStream();\n    ImmediateResponse invalid_mutation_response;\n    invalid_mutation_response.mutable_status()->set_code(StatusCode::InternalServerError);\n    invalid_mutation_response.set_details(std::string(processing_status.message()));\n    sendImmediateResponse(invalid_mutation_response);\n  }\n}\n\nvoid Filter::onGrpcError(Grpc::Status::GrpcStatus status) {\n  ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Received gRPC error on stream: {}\", status);\n  stats_.streams_failed_.inc();\n\n  if (processing_complete_) {\n    return;\n  }\n\n  if (config_->failureModeAllow()) {\n    // Ignore this and treat as a successful close\n    onGrpcClose();\n    stats_.failure_mode_allowed_.inc();\n\n  } else {\n    processing_complete_ = true;\n    // Since the stream failed, there is no need to handle timeouts, so\n    // make sure that they do not fire errorResponse.set_details(absl::StrFormat(\"%s_gRPC_error_%i\", ErrorPrefix, status));\n    sendImmediateResponse(errorResponse);\n  }\n}\n\nvoid Filter::onGrpcClose() {\n  ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Received encoding_state_.onFinishProcessorCall(call_status);\n}\n\nvoid Filter::sendImmediateResponse(const ImmediateResponse& response) {\n  if (config_->isUpstream()) {\n   "file": {
    "content": ".. _config_http_filters_ext_proc:\n\nExternal Processing\n===================\n* This filter should be configured with the type URL ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor``.\n* :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`\n\nThe external processing filter connects an external service, called an \"external processor,\"\nto the filter chain. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\nit to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\nand modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n\nThe protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\nexternal processor\n:ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\nmessages, and the processor must reply with\n:ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\nmessages.\n\nConfiguration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\nThis way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\nrequest and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\non a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\nthat decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\nstream requests from the proxy.\n\nThis filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\nare complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\nbe found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\n\nStatistics\n----------\nThis filter outputs statistics in the\n``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\n<envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\ncomes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\n\nThe following statistics are supported:\n\n.. csv-table::\n  :header: Name, Type, Description\n  :widths: auto\n\n  streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\n  streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\n  streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\n  spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\n  streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\n  streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\n  failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\n  message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\n  rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\n  clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\n  clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear cache requests that were rejected from being disabled\n",

Envoy sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\n// 2. The service sends back a ProcessingResponse message that directs Envoy\n//    to either stop processing, continue without it, or send it the\n//    next chunk of the message body.\n// 3. If so requested, Envoy sends the server chunks of the message body,\n//    or the entire body at once. In either case, the server sends back\n//    a ProcessingResponse after each message it receives.\n// 4. If so requested, Envoy sends the server the HTTP trailers,\n//    and the server sends back a ProcessingResponse.\n// 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again\n//    at step 1 when Envoy receives a response from the upstream server.\n// 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly,\n//    then Envoy proceeds without consulting the server.\n// 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error,\n//    then Envoy returns a 500 error to the client, unless the filter\n//    was configured to ignore errors.\n//\n// In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but\n// using a gRPC stream to make it easier for the server to\n// maintain state.\n\nservice ExternalProcessor {\n  // This begins the bidirectional stream that Envoy will use to\n  // give the server control over what the filter does.
